<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_49d97cb4-ef55-49cc-8794-91a06959054e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<div id="review_190723133" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/190723133" />
    <a title="Derek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5897370-derek"><img alt="Derek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353598576p2/5897370.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/190723133?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Derek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Derek" href="/user/show/5897370-derek">Derek</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316037860" href="/book/show/9435933-the-rogue">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer190723133" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16250794402597503515">Ugh. Where to begin? It was about three years ago that I read the Black Magician's trilogy. It was quite good. When the Magician's Apprentice came out I read it with glee. It was pretty good. And then Canavan began "The Traitor Spy Trilogy". What was she thinking? <br/><br/>The first book in the series, "The Ambassador's Mission" Takes place 20 years after those in the Black Magician Trilogy. It was an okay story, but most of it was spent attempting to recover lost history, history the reader is aware of </span>
  <span id="freeText16250794402597503515" style="display:none">Ugh. Where to begin? It was about three years ago that I read the Black Magician's trilogy. It was quite good. When the Magician's Apprentice came out I read it with glee. It was pretty good. And then Canavan began "The Traitor Spy Trilogy". What was she thinking? <br /><br />The first book in the series, "The Ambassador's Mission" Takes place 20 years after those in the Black Magician Trilogy. It was an okay story, but most of it was spent attempting to recover lost history, history the reader is aware of if they read "The Magician's Apprentice." Oh well, it was still a good story, even if a bit redundant. <br /><br /> When "The Rogue" came out I had to read it. I checked it out from the library (planning on buying it when it came out in paperback) and was glad that I didn't shell out the cash for a hard cover.. This story doesn't resolve anything from the previous books. <br /><br />One of my favorite character's has been Dannyl. I thought that Canavan did a great job with this homosexual character - until now. Now he's torn between loving two men, all the while worried about how old and wrinkly he is. <br /><br />Canavan also adds a new character, who happens to be a lesbian. I have nothing wrong with an author using homosexual characters (Waren from Patricia Briggs "Mercy Thompson" Series is an all time fave character of mine), yet when they introduce that character to further an agenda I begin to get a bit queasy. If the story that Canavan presents would have had some resolutions and gains, I could have been okay with this. As it is, I'm quite disappointed. <br /><br />To Canavan's credit, I did not notice any of the inconsistencies of history that I've noticed in her other works. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16250794402597503515" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_512008419" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/512008419" />
    <a title="Ferdy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy"><img alt="Ferdy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487898103p2/4596358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/512008419?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ferdy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ferdy" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy">Ferdy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=blah-romance">blah-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=boring">boring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=boring-crap-hero">boring-crap-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=blah">blah</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=magic">magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer512008419" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13225794260556682115"><b>Spoilers</b><br/><br/>This was a chore to read, it was boring and slow paced. The characters and arcs didn't hold my interest. <br/>I didn't care about Lorkin or the Traitors, there was nothing remotely entertaining about either of them. Also, Lorkin's relationship with Tyvara was dull.<br/>The addition of Lillia was annoying. She would have been a half decent protagonist but her stupidity and naivety ruined her character. I lost count of the number of times she was manipulated, if she'd been used once or twice that wo</span>
  <span id="freeText13225794260556682115" style="display:none"><b>Spoilers</b><br /><br />This was a chore to read, it was boring and slow paced. The characters and arcs didn't hold my interest. <br />I didn't care about Lorkin or the Traitors, there was nothing remotely entertaining about either of them. Also, Lorkin's relationship with Tyvara was dull.<br />The addition of Lillia was annoying. She would have been a half decent protagonist but her stupidity and naivety ruined her character. I lost count of the number of times she was manipulated, if she'd been used once or twice that would have been forgivable but she never learnt her lesson and she kept letting people use and abuse her, it irritated the hell out of me. I actually liked Naki more — she had attitude and was cunning. Naki's POV would have been far more engaging than plank like Lillia's. <br />Dannyl was awful. He was a likeable character in the Black Magician trilogy but in this one he turned into a stuck up, useless bore that only cared about his love life. All he did was moan about Tayend and how he didn't fancy him anymore and how he wanted to have sex with that other guy. I would have preferred more focus on his research and him making an effort to discover different aspects of magic. There was no adventure or excitement in his search for the history of magic… I had to force myself to read his dull chapters. <br />Sonea was the only decent character. Sadly, she was given a crap arc, all she did was 1. Worry about Lorkin 2. Go to the hospital to work 3. Meet Cery in secret 4. Angst about Dorrien and his wife and 5. Wonder about Regin, his family and how much he's changed.<br />Disappointing. The plot wasn't all bad but the bland characters made everything so boring.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13225794260556682115" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_166567307" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/166567307" />
    <a title="Wai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4492976-wai"><img alt="Wai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1531754734p2/4492976.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/166567307?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wai" href="/user/show/4492976-wai">Wai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11138515-the-rogue">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer166567307" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer422188917065295657">This is a hard book to review. Whilst I did enjoy a lot of it, it also suffered from middle book syndrome in that the main plot isn't even close to being resolved. Obviously, if it had been wrapped up, then there'd be no trilogy, would there? Don't answer that.<br/><br/>So after the events at the end of the last, the two main points are that everyone is desperately searching for Skellin and Lorkin has been taken to the home of the Traitors. If you don't know what I'm talking about, then you're starting in</span>
  <span id="freeText422188917065295657" style="display:none">This is a hard book to review. Whilst I did enjoy a lot of it, it also suffered from middle book syndrome in that the main plot isn't even close to being resolved. Obviously, if it had been wrapped up, then there'd be no trilogy, would there? Don't answer that.<br /><br />So after the events at the end of the last, the two main points are that everyone is desperately searching for Skellin and Lorkin has been taken to the home of the Traitors. If you don't know what I'm talking about, then you're starting in the wrong place and need to go back and read The Ambassador's Mission. Whilst not necessary, I'd also recommend reading the Black Magician trilogy as this involves the same characters some twenty years later.<br /><br />Let me get what I didn't like about the story out of the way and that essentially boils down to lack of progress in the Skellin plotline. Granted I didn't expect much progress but I would have liked to have seen some. In fact, Skellin didn't make an appearance at all. There's that and also the fact that there was little action. A couple of pages over brief fights and a brief kidnapping but they were resolved too quickly.<br /><br />Now that that's out of the way, here's what I did like. We're introduced to a new character, Lilia a novice whose family were servants. I really liked this story line and found myself rooting for her as she falls under the sway of another novice, Naki, an apparent beauty from the upper classes of society. Lilia is seen to grow in character as she comes to terms with her sexuality and her love with Naki which may or may not be returned as well as the life changing events thrust upon her as she encounters the forbidden art of black magic.<br /><br />It might be said that Lilia is a token nod to the lesbian community perhaps to balance out that we already have Dannyl who is openly gay. Whatever the reason that Lilia was introduced, I felt that her story was deftly handled and hopefully we'll see more of her in The Traitor Queen.<br /><br />Lorkin's time amongst the Traitors also advances nicely as he is put to work in an attempt to pay for his father's not honouring his part of a deal. It was good to see the Traitor's society expanded upon, having first met them in The Magician's Apprentice (a prequel to the entire series - another book that is not necessary but will certainly enrich the world).<br /><br />Finally, there is Sonea, the heroine from the Black Magician trilogy, a black magician herself and how comes to terms with a face from the past and at the same time handling the search for Skellin.<br /><br />Overall, it's not a rivetting read, but if you enjoy Trudi Canavan's work and picked up The Ambassor's Mission, then this should be an enjoyable read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="422188917065295657" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_433896893" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/433896893" />
    <a title="Ella" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11487183-ella"><img alt="Ella" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/433896893?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ella" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ella" href="/user/show/11487183-ella">Ella</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer433896893" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5967791045357060851">I think I'm being generous here, another lackluster installment of the traitor spy trilogy only my love of the BMT is keeping me reading in the vain hope that they might improve. <br/>Alas never has a piece of work been such a lead-up to it's next installment since I saw pirates of the Caribbean 2. <br/>There is hardly any action in the book, a look at the Duna tribe was about the hi-light of the entire thing for me. Stick to your strengths Canavan, you're excellent at world-building not so much at creati</span>
  <span id="freeText5967791045357060851" style="display:none">I think I'm being generous here, another lackluster installment of the traitor spy trilogy only my love of the BMT is keeping me reading in the vain hope that they might improve. <br />Alas never has a piece of work been such a lead-up to it's next installment since I saw pirates of the Caribbean 2. <br />There is hardly any action in the book, a look at the Duna tribe was about the hi-light of the entire thing for me. Stick to your strengths Canavan, you're excellent at world-building not so much at creating likable multi-dimensional characters. <br /><br />Lorkin is still a wet blanket and hasn't gotten any brighter as far as I can tell, in fact someone should do a study between the correlation of magical powers and dropping IQ in this world. Anyhoo the traitors have turned out to be exactly the kind of obnoxious, hypocritical straw-feminists I feared...ohh...so close and yet so far away...and back at the guild the whole Naki/Lilia plot is unfortunately such a large chunk of the book I can't skim over it. A lot of people I have seen on here discussed depiction of homosexuality in the book and I honestly think Canavan should just leave it out. Now don't get me wrong I'm not homophobic and loved the Dannyl/Tayend relationship, you know after I grudgingly accepted that Dannyl would never be mine....she seems to have struck gold with her portrayal of their relationship, it was heartwarming, affectionate and the most believable in the whole series, all in all kudos, also even though they were gay it wasn't their ONLY personality trait which often happens in fantasy literature portraying homosexual characters. But after seeing her handle a few more same-sex relationships I realize that the Dannyl/Tayend one was a fluke and she accidentally wrote a believable relationship. In her books the gay characters seem to pair off with each other ONLY because they are gay and no other reason, if there are two gay characters in the same vicinity they will try to screw each other..eh...pretty sure that's not how people work Canavan....<br />I'm blonde and I'm studying to be a geneticist, but I'm not going to jump into bed with the first blonde-haired geneticist I meet, and in fact we'd probably have more in common that most of her paired-off characters....not that her heterosexual pairings are much better Lorkin loves Tyvara at first sight well...because...uhhh....*drools* (that's how I imagine his reasoning anyway) and she seems to reciprocate, just because.<br /><br />And I know this goes beyond this particular book but the magicians, good lord the magicians! Are starting to piss me off. This entire world has a very black and white mentality. Magicians come in two flavours slow-witted and well-meaning “good” magicians who pat themselves on the back for being pillars of the community and are afraid of anything new and different and “bad” magicians who are cartoonishly-evil bond-esque villains who commit evil for fun and profit and try to set themselves up as tyrants or invade countries. As a consequence my favourite character in this book was Naki, yes, she may have been a supremely selfish, manipulative bitch who seduced a naive idiot so that she could frame her all so that she could do what she wanted without being restrained by the guild. She didn't want to take over the country, she didn't want to live in a cave and become queen of the morlocks or anything, she just wanted to have fun with her powers, she was also smarter than most of the other characters until she did her villain monologue at the end and then I knew she was doomed. I’m not asking for evil magicians all I’m asking is for a little more grey, like perhaps a magician whose a perfectly swell guy but doesn't cry himself to sleep every night if he occasionally uses his fireballs to I don’t know, blast a mugger who tried to attack him, or you know, They fight crime!! these people spend the bulk of their adolescence being carefully educated in the ways of magic so that they can…uhh…can…what exactly is it they DO? Aaannd they get a "generous allowance" from the king for doing it, good lord their magical civil servants<br /><br /><br />Ok, so I got a little sidetracked there. The book is so-so, not good, not bad I'm disappointed in it but just know I'm going to end up reading the traitor Queen, i'm 2/3rds of the way in now, might as well stick it out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5967791045357060851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_447610958" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/447610958" />
    <a title="Allison" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9371994-allison"><img alt="Allison" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461856985p2/9371994.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/447610958?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Allison" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Allison" href="/user/show/9371994-allison">Allison</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11369521-the-rogue">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Die-hard Canavan fans with patience</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=published-2010s">published-2010s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=witches-wizards-mages">witches-wizards-mages</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=cliffhanger">cliffhanger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9371994-allison?shelf=thieves">thieves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer447610958" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14080144379967957101">Let me start out by saying this was a vast improvement over the first book in the <i>Traitor Spy Trilogy</i>. In <i>The Rogue</i>, events finally start moving beyond reminiscing about the past and setting the stage. Sort of. The stage is still being set, but it's a wider stage than in <i>The Ambassador's Mission</i>. The focus is less on how Imardin has changed in the last 20 years and how Sonea has been a virtual prisoner and more on current events in Imardin and Sachaka. That alone made it more interesting to read</span>
  <span id="freeText14080144379967957101" style="display:none">Let me start out by saying this was a vast improvement over the first book in the <i>Traitor Spy Trilogy</i>. In <i>The Rogue</i>, events finally start moving beyond reminiscing about the past and setting the stage. Sort of. The stage is still being set, but it's a wider stage than in <i>The Ambassador's Mission</i>. The focus is less on how Imardin has changed in the last 20 years and how Sonea has been a virtual prisoner and more on current events in Imardin and Sachaka. That alone made it more interesting to read, and I didn't struggle through this one. <br /><br />But, this is still a slow mover. There's not much action. It's still very much an exploration of the characters, their daily lives and their thoughts and feelings about small events. It's also still very much a two-track plot. I'm not sure if the events in Imardin and Sachaka will meet up at some point, but right now they seem to be very separate stories. <br /><br />It was good to see Sonea making some of the changes that I'd wished to see in the last book (less emphasis on the over-protective mother hen), and to dive back into Cery's underworld again. I had a hard time with Dannyl's part because I was still stuck on not liking what happened between him and Tayend (I like to believe in true and everlasting love - silly me), but his research did add something of interest.<br /><br />The new characters get more interesting as well. Lorkin is no longer a fuzzy character. He gains a personality and opens up a new world by letting us see the Traitor's colony. We also meet a naive new Novice to bring crisis back to the Guild. <br /><br />Probably only true Canavan fans will be pleased enough to stick it out to the final book of the trilogy - and they are probably the only ones who will read this book anyway. I am one of those. I persevered beyond the first book myself because I had to believe it would get better. And it did, but it still doesn't match up to her previous two trilogies, both of which are among my favorites.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14080144379967957101" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_178973938" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/178973938" />
    <a title="Lord Nouda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5279778-lord-nouda"><img alt="Lord Nouda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338903453p2/5279778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/178973938?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lord Nouda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lord Nouda" href="/user/show/5279778-lord-nouda">Lord Nouda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5279778-lord-nouda?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5279778-lord-nouda?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer178973938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2097406704908842743">It was a bit annoying due to the fact that there's a lot of unnecessary factors in the book. It would seem as though Trudi Canavan is seriously trying to put the spotlight on the homosexual community in the series, and that's even more pronounced in this book where she introduces not just two but 3 entirely new characters (all chicks) who have the hots for each other (or so they claim). In the last book, it was the guys, now it's the opposite side of the spectrum. So out of all the characters in</span>
  <span id="freeText2097406704908842743" style="display:none">It was a bit annoying due to the fact that there's a lot of unnecessary factors in the book. It would seem as though Trudi Canavan is seriously trying to put the spotlight on the homosexual community in the series, and that's even more pronounced in this book where she introduces not just two but 3 entirely new characters (all chicks) who have the hots for each other (or so they claim). In the last book, it was the guys, now it's the opposite side of the spectrum. So out of all the characters in the trilogy, that brings the count up to 6 so far (all main or highly significant to the plotline). That's definitely not a coincidence and I find it distasteful. If this is the type of writing she's going to pursue in the future, I'm pretty sure this will be the last book of hers that I will read.<br /><br />Too much of the book was taken up by the pursuit of their "feelings" for each other. However I was more interested in the magical aspect of the Sachakans and more about black magic in general and especially about the special magic the Traitors practised that wasn't known to the rest of the magical world. There was a half-hearted attempt at injecting the normal type of relations (with the opposite sex) but it turned out to be a flop and highlighted the fact the romance factor in the Traitor Spy trilogy will consist solely of characters of the same Gender.<br /><br />This book was far better than the first and would have been a 4-star if it hadn't been for the facts I highlighted in the past two paragraphs. There's a tipping point where such matters go from "tolerable" and amusing to being simply annoying and Trudi has gone past it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2097406704908842743" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1130169612" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1130169612" />

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11138515-the-rogue">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26734926-emma?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26734926-emma?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer17632651969483210564">It's been a long time since I last visited Sonea and co. in this series, and I was not disappointed. This novel introduced a new central character- a young, female novice named Lilia, who falls in with the wrong crowd early in the story. It was great to introduce some new blood into this series, and Lilia provided a fish-out-of-water perspective that Sonea had previously represented in the original trilogy. <br/><br/>Meanwhile, the rest of our main characters' plots carried on in much the same manner as i</span>
  <span id="freeText17632651969483210564" style="display:none">It's been a long time since I last visited Sonea and co. in this series, and I was not disappointed. This novel introduced a new central character- a young, female novice named Lilia, who falls in with the wrong crowd early in the story. It was great to introduce some new blood into this series, and Lilia provided a fish-out-of-water perspective that Sonea had previously represented in the original trilogy. <br /><br />Meanwhile, the rest of our main characters' plots carried on in much the same manner as in the previous book. Sonea is hunting a rogue magician in the city, while her son Lorkin lives as a prisoner in a faraway land. The final storyline revolves around Dannyl and his research/love life. Unfortunately his was by far the least interesting, which is a shame, as Dannyl was one of my favourite characters in the original novel. <br /><br />This is a must read for fans of the original series- I'd forgotten how fond I was of all of the characters.</span>

<div id="review_167061020" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167061020" />
    <a title="Julia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1136388-julia"><img alt="Julia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305029288p2/1136388.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167061020?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julia" href="/user/show/1136388-julia">Julia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1136388-julia?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167061020" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4171771717455489962">I've read this one twice. Once very quickly, skipping through a LOT, and once carefully, trying not to skip as much. <br/><br/>My opinion, though very bad at first, has slightly changed. It's better than I first thought it was. You can see how it's a middle book, but it has interesting scenes. <br/>One thing I've never liked about Trudi Canavan was the romances in her books… and I still think they're sometimes quite ridiculous, but that might just be my opinion. There are scenes that I was not sure whether to </span>
  <span id="freeText4171771717455489962" style="display:none">I've read this one twice. Once very quickly, skipping through a LOT, and once carefully, trying not to skip as much. <br /><br />My opinion, though very bad at first, has slightly changed. It's better than I first thought it was. You can see how it's a middle book, but it has interesting scenes. <br />One thing I've never liked about Trudi Canavan was the romances in her books… and I still think they're sometimes quite ridiculous, but that might just be my opinion. There are scenes that I was not sure whether to laugh at or to cry about, but all in all, there are worse things. I am still disappointed, especially because many things seemed obvious or even too plot-directed.<br /><br />In general, she repeats a lot of information. Yes, it's the nature of different viewpoints, but somehow, it just gets tedious. <br /><br />Now, on to SPOILERS.<br />***WARNING, WARNING, WARNING, DON'T READ IF YOU DON'T WANT TO BE SPOILERED***<br /><br />Well, not plot-relevant, but still might spoiling some: I was surprised at how the book features 5 clearly gay characters and one… of which at this point is not clear whether she is gay or whether she faked being gay. And it's both male and female. <br />I've liked Trudi Canavan for it in BMT. It was way underdone, but it was there, at the very least. Now, after "The Magician's Apprentice" and the traitor spy trilogy, I think that if she was planning to make it such a big part of her books, then she could have done it better. On the other hand, I'll be shipping… the last couple to kiss in the book… from now on, so I don't think it's too bad. Also, middle aged gay men are a rare sight and kudos to her for making it realistic. <br /><br />Lorkin, also, was more bearable, although… although it was hard to get through a few of his thoughts. In general, I found it tedious to plough through some of the bits. <br /><br />Most disappointed I am at how little Dannyl/Tayend interaction was in the book… In fact, given what was in the book, I have a nagging feeling Canavan might kill one of the two. But I have, of course, no real reason to believe that and there is absolutely no proof or reason to worry. I've just contemplated about it. <br />But the real reason I'm upset is because there's hardly any dialogue… I'd have liked to better understand the two. I know they're supposed to be drifting apart, but Canavan has failed (to me) in doing it in a way that I still find Dannyl sympathetic. <br /><br />***SPOILERS END HERE***<br /><br />All in all, I will continue reading. Because I want to know what the conclusion or the big drama is. Because Canavan's strengths lie in the last books. Because I guess I'm still hooked on a few characters. <br />I was disappointed, overall, but not overly. It's a middle book, after all, and there are a few very interesting things about the world which make the read entertaining. And, hey, it got me thinking about the story for a whole day, even if it wasn't in the most positive light. <br />Those who love Trudi Canavan's style will certainly learn to enjoy it, even if no eternal love may blossom. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4171771717455489962" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_645627354" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/645627354" />
    <a title="Maurine Tritch" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1220877-maurine-tritch"><img alt="Maurine Tritch" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601591074p2/1220877.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/645627354?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maurine Tritch" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maurine Tritch" href="/user/show/1220877-maurine-tritch">Maurine Tritch</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer645627354" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13790013094778627944">This book suffers from the same affliction as the first installment in the series: it was too long for the material. There were too many scenes that didn't need to be there, that only serve as a bit of unnecessary character development and did nothing to advance the plot. The worst offender is the thread where a naive novice is introduced who is lead astray by an older girl, and it is blindingly obvious what was going on almost immediately. There is no need to take us in detail through the whole</span>
  <span id="freeText13790013094778627944" style="display:none">This book suffers from the same affliction as the first installment in the series: it was too long for the material. There were too many scenes that didn't need to be there, that only serve as a bit of unnecessary character development and did nothing to advance the plot. The worst offender is the thread where a naive novice is introduced who is lead astray by an older girl, and it is blindingly obvious what was going on almost immediately. There is no need to take us in detail through the whole relationship from their first meeting onwards. Ditto for the odd almost romance with Sonea and her married healer friend; far too much concentrated time is spent on something that ultimately didn't matter and also failed to provide any real tension or doubt. It should have been very much a background to action. The novel was also hurt because it was so choppy. There is a ton of points of view that are followed throughout and each lasts for only a couple of pages at the most, often only paragraphs. You just get a sense of the change in scenery and remember what the characters there are doing and you're whisked off somewhere else almost immediately.<br /><br />That being said, I very much enjoyed seeing the culture of the Traitors, the hidden, rebel society run by women; and the sections with Dannyl were interesting as he juggled his precarious role as ambassador and personal concerns. I also didn't mind the story of the hapless novice once it moved past the painfully predictable.<br /><br />I am most interested in Regin, Sonea's childhood tormenter, about what he's really up now to and what his motivations are in the supportive help he's been offering her. Unfortunately he was basically absent in this book, but I am hoping for a resolution in the next one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13790013094778627944" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8966725853825837665"> did not enjoy this book nearly as much as I had hoped. It is not like I hated it, but I found it to be very dull. I couldn't get into Trudi Canavan's writing style at all and the way she kept jumping from character to character to character annoyed me. I never managed to know or care about them, though several seemed like they could be interesting if given the opportunity.<br/><br/>Lilia, for example. She is a gentle, naive girl just learning about love and she is led to do a foolish, dangerous thing. In</span>
  <span id="freeText8966725853825837665" style="display:none"> did not enjoy this book nearly as much as I had hoped. It is not like I hated it, but I found it to be very dull. I couldn't get into Trudi Canavan's writing style at all and the way she kept jumping from character to character to character annoyed me. I never managed to know or care about them, though several seemed like they could be interesting if given the opportunity.<br /><br />Lilia, for example. She is a gentle, naive girl just learning about love and she is led to do a foolish, dangerous thing. Instead of shirking her responsibilities or trying to hide, she faces what she did wrong and does her best to make it right, even though it may cost her what she holds most dear. I could respect and like her for that, but since the characters kept switching around I never really got to know her.<br /><br />Lorkin also had some potential, as did Anyi. Cery bothered me because in the first book his family was murdered in the first chapter and other than one bout of tears he didn't show any emotion. Their deaths were only mentioned every so often in a half-hearted and ineffectual attempt to elicit an emotional response from the reader. Sonea was completely bland and Dannyl...I had trouble paying attention to his storyline because I was so bored.<br /><br />The plot moved very slowly with nothing unexpected or original coming up. Despite all of this, I must confess to a mild curiosity as to how it will end. Perhaps when book 3 comes out I will read the last 5 pages. But not the whole book.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://liedermadchen.blogspot.com/2011/07/book-review-83-rogue-by-trudi-canavan.html">http://liedermadchen.blogspot.com/201...</a></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/397822315?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauren" href="/user/show/3510704-lauren">Lauren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer397822315" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12885479497507423736">**SPOILER ALERT**<br/><br/>I much preferred this book to the previous installment in the Traitor Spy Trilogy, 'The Ambassador's Mission'. I felt that this book focused more on the characters we know and love, and was much more exciting and fast paced. I also loved references and parallels to th Black Magician Trilogy - especially the waterfall! ;) :')<br/><br/>The only thing I really don't like about this book is Dannyl and Tayend. Now. I fell in love with Dannyl in the first book, and when I found out he was gay i</span>
  <span id="freeText12885479497507423736" style="display:none">**SPOILER ALERT**<br /><br />I much preferred this book to the previous installment in the Traitor Spy Trilogy, 'The Ambassador's Mission'. I felt that this book focused more on the characters we know and love, and was much more exciting and fast paced. I also loved references and parallels to th Black Magician Trilogy - especially the waterfall! ;) :')<br /><br />The only thing I really don't like about this book is Dannyl and Tayend. Now. I fell in love with Dannyl in the first book, and when I found out he was gay it broke my heart. I've just gotten used to the fact that Tayend 'stole' him from me, and was actually rather starting to like them as a couple - now, in this series, their relationship has fallen apart and Dannyl is looking elsewhere! I'm sorry, but Dannyl would never look at anyone other than Tayend. Never.They loved each other so much. I love Trudi Canavan, but this just doesn't seem likely to me. I'm hoping for a reconciliation (and no Dannyl/Achati action!) in the next book.<br /><br />The Black Magician trilogy is one of my favourite series of all time, and very few books have ever lived up to it for me. As much as I love Canavan's work and am enjoying this series at the moment, I don't think it will ever be able to recapture the magic of BMT. Nothing ever will. But I did read this book in one sitting and got straight online to order the next one, so I would definitely recommend it to fans of BMT.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12885479497507423736" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/494656989" />
    <a title="Lindsey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3349617-lindsey"><img alt="Lindsey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1267223483p2/3349617.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/494656989?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lindsey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lindsey" href="/user/show/3349617-lindsey">Lindsey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316037846" href="/book/show/12625176-the-rogue">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3349617-lindsey?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer494656989" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12067376687206104782">Better than its predecessor, Canavan gets and keep the plot rolling through the entire book. I liked the introduction of Lilia to the cast, as we haven't had a Novice in this mix yet. (Although it's actually nice that the majority of the protagonists in this trilogy are middle-aged.) The plot moved much more steadily and continues to not revolve around the magical abilities of the characters as a device to move forward.<br/><br/>The aspect I continued to have the most trouble with, however, is connecting </span>
  <span id="freeText12067376687206104782" style="display:none">Better than its predecessor, Canavan gets and keep the plot rolling through the entire book. I liked the introduction of Lilia to the cast, as we haven't had a Novice in this mix yet. (Although it's actually nice that the majority of the protagonists in this trilogy are middle-aged.) The plot moved much more steadily and continues to not revolve around the magical abilities of the characters as a device to move forward.<br /><br />The aspect I continued to have the most trouble with, however, is connecting emotionally to the characters. It's a bit like a friend telling you a distressing story about someone you've never met. You know it must be horrible for them but you only sporadically connect their emotions with yours. There's nothing flawed in the storytelling per se, it's just my preference that I feel what the characters are experiencing.<br /><br />Despite that, the story is engaging and I particularly appreciate Canavan's ability to portray all styles of relationships, from mentors and friends and lovers to the more ambiguous, could/should questions that come up in real life. I also like that her characters make intelligent choices and live with them, even when they're working on flawed information. There's a lot to admire in who her characters are as people, which is a nice change from much of what I've read lately.<br /><br />Recommended to Canavan's fans and general fantasy readers. Easily appropriate for teens as well, for those who are concerned with content warnings.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12067376687206104782" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16012363750365235088">As I suspected / hoped, this was more exciting than the Ambassador's Mission.   <span id="freeText16012363750365235088" style="display:none">As I suspected / hoped, this was more exciting than the Ambassador's Mission. There was more action, and though it wasn't exactly fast-paced it was at least faster paced than the first book.<br /><br />What I didn't really like was Lilias storyline. It would've been way better, if Naki's malicious intents hadn't been so obvious I think... Because the way we were introduced to Lilia, we quickly realized how stupid and impressionable she was, which made me dislike her. Though I have to say, she's grown on me a little in the end. I'm very curious to see where the third book leads her and Anyi's relationship (who, by the way, is amazing and super badass *-*). <br />Also, Dorrien was still in love with Sonea? I find that hard to believe, after 20 years of mostly living apart. Makes him seem a little pathetic, which is a shame, because I quite liked him.<br />I'm super excited for what will happen between Dannyl and Achati in the next book. I don't really like the way his and Tayend's relationship ended (after 20 years of being together, they just shrug it off??), but he and Achati are off to a promising start. Who doesn't like a little slow burn romance? ;D<br />As far as Lorkin's storyline goes... I'm not sure yet if I like it - or him. Which is probably because he can't really have his own agenda, instead he is pushed by circumstances to do what's more often than not the only way to survive. All the while being infatuated with Tyvara. What a guy!^^<br /><br />I'm still excited for book three, though. I'm hoping for a big finale, and though it's not perfect, I still like the characters and their world :)</span>

<div id="review_307259052" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/307259052" />
    <a title="Becky (Blogs of a Bookaholic)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8613391-becky-blogs-of-a-bookaholic"><img alt="Becky (Blogs of a Bookaholic)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529956761p2/8613391.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/307259052?book_show_action=true">Apr 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky (Blogs of a Bookaholic)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky (Blogs of a Bookaholic)" href="/user/show/8613391-becky-blogs-of-a-bookaholic">Becky (Blogs of a Bookaholic)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Existing fans of The Black Magician Trilogy</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8613391-becky-blogs-of-a-bookaholic?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer307259052" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13977235631266138851"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404251280i/10214586.png' width='400' height='171' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>This review was originally published on <a href='http://beckysblogs.wordpress.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blogs of a Bookaholic</a>.<br/><br/><b>An enjoyable meander around the world of Kyralia that lacked some of the fire of Canavan’s previous works.</b><br/>This book felt a little like an overindulgent chess game. There are sets of characters on each side of the board in the lands of Kyralia and Sachaka, and the story flits back and forth between the two. With <i>Canvan’s</i> key characters spread so widely it really slowed down the plot. Each time the reader visits a different character a </span>
  <span id="freeText13977235631266138851" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404251280i/10214586.png" width="400" height="171" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This review was originally published on <a href="http://beckysblogs.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blogs of a Bookaholic</a>.<br><br><b>An enjoyable meander around the world of Kyralia that lacked some of the fire of Canavan’s previous works.</b><br>This book felt a little like an overindulgent chess game. There are sets of characters on each side of the board in the lands of Kyralia and Sachaka, and the story flits back and forth between the two. With <i>Canvan’s</i> key characters spread so widely it really slowed down the plot. Each time the reader visits a different character a small nugget of information is revealed or a question is posed, as if moving a tiny chess piece one space forward on the board. The problem is, these pieces of information are so minuscule that it takes a long time to learn anything substantial, furthermore, each time one small piece of information is found the characters have to mull it over and over again each time you revisit them to decide where they’re going to move their chess piece next. While I enjoyed each story individually because of my long affection for the world <i>Canavan</i> had created and was happy to let the book plod along at a slow pace, the plotting prevented this book from being anything extraordinary. <br><br>As always I found <i>Canvan’s</i> writing wonderful to read and this was by far my favourite aspect of the book. Her prose felt smooth and delicate, without realising it 50 pages of <i>The Rogue</i> could fly by with no problem, even considering the slow plotting. I loved <i>Canavan’s</i> imagery especially, the descriptions of the Sachakan desert transported me, and her vision for the Traitor’s safe haven was a brilliant mix of imagination and thoughtful practicality.<br><br>I was pleased to see some further character development in this book. I was worried that I wouldn't warm up to Sonea’s son, Lorkin as nothing grabbed me about him in the first novel. His dealings with the Traitor’s society did make him more amiable. He is set challenges that test his morals, giving more insight into his personality, and I am interested to see what he will do and accomplish next. I was also surprised and pleased by the reappearance of Dorrien a favourite character from the previous trilogy. His return while not vital to the plot in any way was still a lot of fun. Sonea was her same old stoical and endearing self which I always enjoy reading. However, the storyline given to her in this book was really quite lackluster, and she seemed to miss obvious evidence that was right under her nose which led to a bit of frustration. <br>There were also new additions to the series, two novices Naki and Lilia. I thought they could add an interesting new element and I liked the emphasis on the collision of class differences. However, the storyline soon became predictable, not to mention irritating. Lilia was frustratingly naïve and put her trust in the most ridiculous people. At first I liked her character, but by the end of the novel I wanted to whack her over the head with a stick Rafiki style.<br><br>Although I have listed a lot of negatives I did enjoy this book, it was a fun bit of relief and relaxation in comparison to the real world! I guess this review reflects my frustration with the series, especially as I know <i>Trudi Canavan</i> is capable of far bigger and better things. I can only hope that the third book will bring an action filled worthwhile ending that I know the author is capable of! <br><br><b>You can check out my full, unabridged review and others like it <a href="http://beckysblogs.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blogs of a Bookaholic</a>. :)</b> </span>
  <a data-text-id="13977235631266138851" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1548172416" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1548172416" />
    <a title="zachary" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23021245-zachary"><img alt="zachary" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588167716p2/23021245.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1548172416?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="zachary" class="user" itemprop="url" name="zachary" href="/user/show/23021245-zachary">zachary</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316037846" href="/book/show/12625176-the-rogue">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to zachary by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/50391030-gabriel">Gabriel</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23021245-zachary?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23021245-zachary?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23021245-zachary?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23021245-zachary?shelf=borrowed">borrowed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23021245-zachary?shelf=english">english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23021245-zachary?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23021245-zachary?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23021245-zachary?shelf=epic">epic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1548172416" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4567817429813430676">Lorkin is living with the Traitors' in their safe haven within the mountains of Sachaka. He has been assigned work in the hospital section where he helps healing the sick inhabitants. So far he hasn't had to use magic to heal anyone but he realises it's not going to take long before he's going to need to use magic to save someone's life. But he is just as sure that when that day comes, Kalia is going to everything in her power to make sure the kowledge is shared – even if it will cost lives to m</span>
  <span id="freeText4567817429813430676" style="display:none">Lorkin is living with the Traitors' in their safe haven within the mountains of Sachaka. He has been assigned work in the hospital section where he helps healing the sick inhabitants. So far he hasn't had to use magic to heal anyone but he realises it's not going to take long before he's going to need to use magic to save someone's life. But he is just as sure that when that day comes, Kalia is going to everything in her power to make sure the kowledge is shared – even if it will cost lives to make sure it is.<br /><br />Meanwhile, Lord Dannyl tries to continue his research about the storestone that seems to have been the cause of the wastelands in Sachaka. But suddenly Tayend shows up as the new Ambadassor from Elyne wich is bittersweet – but Dannyl struggles to find the sweetness of it most of the time. Especially when Achati is around... which is often as he seems just as passionate in finding out the truth about the storestone and the wastelands.<br /><br />Back in Kyralia, a young novice by the name Lilia has befriended her beautiful, charming classmate Naki. Lilia is completely and absolutely besotted with her new friend but everything changes one night when Naki suggests they try to learn black magic from a book she found in her father's office...<br /><br />Oh, boy. This book was definitely an improvement from the first book of the series. The new storylines are established and Canavan has already spent so much time reminding the reader of what happened during the first series that there's not really much of it in this one – which truly felt like a blessing. I felt a lot more excited during my read through of this one than book one. I know that book one in a trilogy is the first act of a three act structure but I felt impatient and bored in a way I didn't even feel during te first forty pages of The Fellowship of the Ring.<br /><br />There was a lot of character development in this one and especially Lorkin was given more room to establish himself as a distinct character. But I liked the new characters as well; even if Lilia had me groaning more than once or twice. There was a lot of Anyi in this one which was very much appreciated and hopefully she can teach Lilia a thing or two by the next book. God knows that girl needs it. <br /><br />Although despite her obvious lack of judgement and her severe naivety, I liked this subplot quite a lot. It gave more insight to the life of the novices and how their lives are affected by everything going on – especially after the events of the previous trilogy. But it was also a good symbolic story for what domestic abuse is like; how it isn't always physical and how hard it is to change one's mindset concerning the abuser as the victim.<br /><br />But most of all, I'm really excited to read the concluding act of this series. I have a feeling it's going to be a really good one. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4567817429813430676" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3376920897" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3376920897" />
    <a title="Veronica Ika " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18173496-veronica-ika"><img alt="Veronica Ika " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566828461p2/18173496.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3376920897?book_show_action=true">Jun 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Veronica Ika " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Veronica Ika " href="/user/show/18173496-veronica-ika">Veronica Ika </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18173496-veronica-ika?shelf=four-stars">four-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18173496-veronica-ika?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18173496-veronica-ika?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18173496-veronica-ika?shelf=high-fantasy">high-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3376920897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12452908385483532441">Reading this second instalment of Traitor Spy trilogy gives me the same excitement I get when I was reading the second instalment of Black Magician trilogy. Much better experience than the first books, both tend to drag and lull you into a deep sleep in some parts. Though this kind of writing style risks to lose the easily discouraged readers from the first books, I’m amazed that Trudi Canavan is able to write better story in the second book and even better in the third book (though I still need</span>
  <span id="freeText12452908385483532441" style="display:none">Reading this second instalment of Traitor Spy trilogy gives me the same excitement I get when I was reading the second instalment of Black Magician trilogy. Much better experience than the first books, both tend to drag and lull you into a deep sleep in some parts. Though this kind of writing style risks to lose the easily discouraged readers from the first books, I’m amazed that Trudi Canavan is able to write better story in the second book and even better in the third book (though I still need to prove the later in this trilogy). After all, there are many trilogies that start with extraordinary first book but lost all the lustre in the middle book.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>GOOD NEWS, BAD NEWS</u>
</b><br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“Our ways are not without flaws. We may not be fair and equal in all things, but we are much closer to that ideal than any other society.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />In the Sanctuary, Lorkin does his best dwelling among the Traitors, following their way of living and rules, in hope they are willing to share the secrets of their unique magic in exchange of learning Healing from him, an unfulfilled promise of his father, Akkarin, to the society. But not only the Traitors are reluctant to trade with him, some of them are inclined to retrieve the skill from him freely, even by force. Can Lorkin, a willing prisoner of Traitors, sacrifice more to accomplish this endeavour?<br /><br />Being the Guild Ambassador to Sachaka turns out to be boring compared to Dannyl’s experience as the Guild Ambassador for Elyne. No ambassadorial duties to attend and no meaningful progress to his attempt to write a complete history book and find a truth behind the missing storestone and the mysterious wasteland. Thankfully, he doesn’t need to be engrossed in his boredom for long. Not when his former lover, Tayend, comes to Sachaka as Elyne’s foreign Ambassador, and obviously wants to interfere with his new love life, who happens to be a very influential Ashaki. Can he put aside his own interest and work with both of them in a journey that is suddenly about everything his role as Ambassador entailed?<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“The Guild hasn’t held a prisoner in years,” Lord Telano muttered. “Suddenly it has two.”</blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Meanwhile, back in Imardin, Sonea’s attempt to search for Skellin bears no fruit. Not only that he is a rogue magician from a foreign land, he is also the most influential Thief and the king of roet. The fact that she has his mother doesn’t truly help, nor the assistance of the Guild and her best friend Cery. To make it worse, two novices have uncovered a secret that should have remained hidden, a secret that can’t be unlearned...<br /><br /><b>There are four POVs in this story:</b> three we know very well (Sonea’s, Lorkin’s, and Dannyl’s) and one new character (Lilia’s). What about Cery? Well, unlike the first book, he won’t narrate his own story this time, even though we will still have him throughout the book. How about Lilia? Frankly speaking, I’m a bit worried the first time her character and POV is introduced. Apparently, she’s by far the most interesting character to follow. Despite her weak traits, her story is not dragging and quite engaging that I reluctant to put the book down. She brings so many novelties to this trilogy: a lesbian relationship with her senior novice, which is also her partner in crime; a shocking truth about black magic; revealing another character’s sexual orientation; even starting a new fashion statement. Her case eventually crosses path with Sonea’s mission, and so both POVs are my favourites. <br /><br />Lorkin’s POV, somehow, even when it’s supposed to be the main POV, considering the title of the trilogy, fails to steal the spotlight. Or maybe because mainly I don’t find the Traitors that interesting. They claim to be a fair and equal society, while ironically, they are actually only another version of Sachaka. While Sachaka is dominated by male black magicians who look down on their women, the Traitors are dominated by female black magicians who look down on their men. They do not teach their men magic, as Ashaki in Sachakan do not their women magic. Their difference is, Traitors do not practice slavery. How can they claim to be equal if they have their queen and Speakers? How can they claim to be fair if they treat their men like a plaything? Fortunately, after his unwanted predicament, the storyline is getting better, and similar to Lilia’s, bring about novelties and unpredictable circumstances.<br /><br />Dannyl’s POV involves novelties, too, even when you exclude the truth about storestone and Sachakan wasteland, which will not be new at all if you have read the prequel, the Magician’s Apprentice. However, his story tends to be outshined by others as it is in the Black Magician trilogy. For me, Dannyl’s POV in this book is the worst I’ve ever read! It’s so boring and irritating until he decides to travel to Duna, which occurs after half of the book! Overall, we should be glad that <b>this book gives us so much new information rather than repetition of the history or past events.</b><br /><br /><b>The story takes an unexpected turn in terms of villain.</b> In the first book, following the capture of Lorandra, a magician from a foreign land, Trudi Canavan hints at the possibility of two villains: Skellin and Black Magician Kallen. In this book, Skellin has proven to be a perfect epitome of true villain: invincible and invisible, while Kallen turns out to be a harmless (except to himself) and pathetic addict. The emergence of a new villain is so unexpected, and though this villain will not make another appearance in the future, we are warned that evil people do not always dream big.<br /><br />One thing that I can’t fathom is Trudi Canavan’s attempt to include LGBT in her works. I do not particularly enjoy it but I’m not against it, too. But reading it in Trudi Canavan’s works, I get the impression that she actually doesn’t really know how to write about it or feel okay to write about it but just goes with it because there is an upward trend in writing LGBT fictions. <b>LGBT in this trilogy, as in the previous trilogy, seems so awkward and forced, especially the gay relationship.</b> We learn that our gay couple (Dannyl and Tayend), which looked the least like a couple in the previous trilogy, is actually living together in the gap of 20 years, and by the time this trilogy is unfold, they break up, and Dannyl desires Achati, an influential Ashaki, who desires him back. So, it’s as if Dannyl goes back to square one, but this time it’s Achati instead of Tayend. No hug, kiss, let alone sex, homosexuality is so extremely subtle as if it doesn’t really exist. Strangely enough, Trudi Canavan seems do it fine with the lesbian relationship firstly introduced in this second instalment: Lilia and Naki and later Lilia and Anyi. Both relationships are very very young, but both already share passionate kisses. Even so, I think having 6 LGBT characters from the initial 2 is too hasty, don’t you agree? <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12452908385483532441" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1413345046" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1413345046" />
    <a title="zuz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37379004-zuz"><img alt="zuz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592238233p2/37379004.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hCOiv/qHqs6/bg2j/ugb20sRNPFwRKGVWdH3IwxxU7hBDjLXcfhxZ5pH4TnaeBa3ET7nu46hw47zbnejXc3Ryg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('tv8vm/eCBJ21KerU0hbBx4OHlbsIEQagbLlh8TS31aFz0r/zfP3fNJAABk72hsyr2ahG8fb0ZLvGBuFxZQtX0w==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/15890.Trudi_Canavan">About Trudi Canavan</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/15890.Trudi_Canavan"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1194378660p3/15890.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/15890.Trudi_Canavan">Trudi Canavan

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4236048283233280264">Trudi Canavan was born in Kew, Melbourne and grew up in Ferntree Gully, a suburb at the foothills of the Dandenongs.<br/><br/>In 1999 she won the Aurealis Award for Best Fantasy Short Story with “Whispers of the Mist Children”. In the same year she was granted a writers residency at Varuna Writers’ Centre in Katoomba, New South Wales.<br/><br/>In November 2001, The Magicians’ Guild was first published in Australia. T</span>
  <span id="freeText4236048283233280264" style="display:none">Trudi Canavan was born in Kew, Melbourne and grew up in Ferntree Gully, a suburb at the foothills of the Dandenongs.<br /><br />In 1999 she won the Aurealis Award for Best Fantasy Short Story with “Whispers of the Mist Children”. In the same year she was granted a writers residency at Varuna Writers’ Centre in Katoomba, New South Wales.<br /><br />In November 2001, The Magicians’ Guild was first published in Australia. The second book of the trilogy, The Novice, was published in June 2002 and was nominated for the Aurealis Award for Best Fantasy Novel. The third book The High Lord was released in January 2003 and was nominated for the Best Novel Ditmar category. All three books entered Australian top ten SF bestseller lists.<br /><br />The Black Magician Trilogy reached the international market in 2004, published by HarperCollins’ EOS imprint in North America and Orbit Books in the UK. The trilogy is now rated by Nielsen BookScan as the most successful debut fantasy series of the last 10 years.<br /><br />Trudi’s second trilogy, Age of the Five, has also enjoyed bestselling success. Priestess of the White reached No.3 in the Sunday Times hardback fiction bestseller list, staying in the top ten for six weeks.<br /><br />In early 2006 Trudi signed a seven-figure contract with Orbit to write the prequel and sequel to the Black Magician Trilogy. The prequel, The Magician’s Apprentice was released in 2009 and won the Best Fantasy Novel category of the Aurealis Awards. She is now working on the sequel trilogy, and planning her next fantasy series, which will be set in an entirely new world.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4236048283233280264" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
